First Objection: Souls Could Be Multiple by Essence
Al-Razi presents the first objection and its refutation, including a circularity argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first objection to the proof of the soul's non-eternity and how al-Razi refutes it by exposing a circularity in Avicenna's reasoning.

Core Idea
Souls could be multiple by essence, not just by accidents.

The first objection challenges the claim that souls cannot be pre-eternal by arguing that souls may be distinguished by their very quiddity rather than by accidental attributes. Al-Razi responds by questioning the premise that accidental distinction requires different material substrates and by exposing a circularity in Avicenna's argument against transmigration.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how the objection presents an alternative possibility: souls could be multiple in pre-eternity by their essence.
The objector uses the term 'mahiyya' (quiddity) to argue that souls may differ intrinsically.
2
Identify the key flaw pointed out by al-Razi
Al-Razi points out that the opponent's argument relies on an unproven claim about accidental distinction requiring different substrates. He then shows a logical circularity in Avicenna's position on transmigration.
The circularity is between the refutation of transmigration and the proof of the soul's origination.
3
Understand the refutation's structure
The refutation has two parts: first, challenging the premise; second, exposing the circularity. See how each part builds on the objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن الاعتراض على هذه الحجة من وجهين :
الوجه الأول في الاعتراض: لا نسلم أنها ليست أزلية ولم لا يجوز أن يقال: إنها في الأزل متعددة، وكان امتياز بعضها عن بعض بنفس الماهية، وقولهم : النفوس البشرية واحدة بالنوع فهو محض الدعوى.
لا يقال : هب أنها ليست واحدة في النوع لكن لاشك أن كل نفس تفرض فإنها قد تحصل نفس أخرى لتساويها في تمام الماهية، وحينئذ يتم الدليل. لأنا نقول : هذا تمسك بالظن، ولم لا يجوز أن يقال: إن كل نفسين موجودين فهما مختلفان بالماهية إلا أن اختلافهما في الماهية لا يمنع من اشتراكهما في صفات كثيرة ؟ وأيضًا لم لا يجوز أن يقال: كل واحد من تلك الأعداد يمتاز بعضها عن بعض بالصفات العرضية ؟ قوله : "التباين بالصفات العرضية لا يحصل إلا بسبب اختلاف المواد" قلنا هذا ممنوع فما الدليل عليه ؟ سلمنا ذلك، لكن لم لا يجوز : أن يقال : النفس قبل تعلقها بهذا البدن كانت ببدن آخر - كما يقوله أصحاب التناسخ ؟ واعلم أن الشيخ أبا علي بن سينا إنما أبطل التناسخ بدليل مبني على حدوث النفس، ودليله على حدوث النفس مبني على بطلان التناسخ - كما بيناه ههنا - فوقع الدور.
وأما الحجة الثانية - وهي قوله : الأرواح لو كانت قديمة لكنا نتذكر الآن شيئًا من الأحوال الماضية - قلنا : هذا تمسك بالاستقراء، وهو ضعيف أيضًا، فلم لا يجوز أن يقال : تذكر النفس للأحوال الماضية مشروط بتعلق النفس بالبدن الذي معه حدثت
Know that the objection to this argument is from two aspects. The first aspect of objection: we do not concede that they (souls) are not pre-eternal. Why may it not be said that they are multiple in pre-eternity, and that their distinction from one another is by the very quiddity (mahiyya)? And their statement that human souls are one in species is pure assertion. It cannot be said: suppose they are not one in species, but there is no doubt that every soul assumed can have another soul equal to it in complete quiddity, and then the proof is complete. For we say: this is clinging to conjecture. Why may it not be said that every two existing souls differ in quiddity, yet their difference in quiddity does not prevent their sharing many attributes? Also, why may it not be said that each one of those units is distinguished from another by accidental attributes? His statement: 'Distinction by accidental attributes occurs only due to difference of matters'—we say this is denied; what is the proof of it? We concede that, but why may it not be said that the soul before its attachment to this body was with another body—as the proponents of transmigration (tanasukh) say? Know that the master Abu Ali ibn Sina indeed refuted transmigration by a proof based on the soul's origination, and his proof of the soul's origination is based on the invalidity of transmigration—as we have explained here—so a circularity occurs. As for the second argument—which is his statement: 'If the spirits were eternal, we would now remember something of the past states'—we say: this is clinging to induction, which is also weak. Why may it not be said that the soul's remembrance of past states is conditioned on the soul's attachment to the body with which it originated?
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage presents two objections (i'tiradan) against the earlier proofs that souls are not pre-eternal and thus not everlasting. The first objection challenges the first proof's claim that souls cannot be multiple in pre-eternity. The objector says: souls could be multiple by their very quiddity, not by accidental attributes; the assertion that human souls are one in species is groundless. Even if they were one in species, they could still be multiple by essence. The author responds by rejecting the claim that quiddity alone distinguishes; he points out that the argument from accidental attributes is based on an unproven premise about matter. He also raises the possibility of transmigration (tanasukh) as a way to have pre-existent souls with bodies, which leads to a circularity in Avicenna's reasoning: his refutation of transmigration assumes the soul's origination, and his proof of origination assumes no transmigration. The second objection attacks the memory argument, saying it relies on induction (istiqra') which is weak; memory might depend on the specific body with which the soul originated, so if the soul had another body before, it might not remember. The text cuts off before the full response.

Key Terms
اعتراض
ماهية
تناسخ
دور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What circularity does al-Razi point out in Avicenna's arguments?
A) Avicenna's proof of the soul's origination relies on the refutation of transmigration, and his refutation of transmigration relies on the soul's origination.
B) Avicenna's arguments are based on revelation, not reason.
C) The circularity is between the soul's pre-eternity and its attachment to the body.
D) Avicenna used the same proof for both the soul's pre-eternity and its origination.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi refutes the first objection by exposing a circular dependency in Avicenna's arguments against transmigration and for the soul's origination.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever clung to an argument simply because it supported your view, without checking if it logically depended on the very conclusion you were trying to prove? Take a moment to examine the foundations of your beliefs about the soul—where might you be assuming what you need to prove?
?
The objector here relies on conjecture (ẓann) instead of certain proof. In your own understanding of matters of the unseen, how often do you settle for plausible-sounding claims rather than demanding solid evidence? What is one area where you have done this, and what would it take to seek certainty?
?
Al-Razi does not hesitate to critique even a great scholar like Ibn Sina. Are you willing to critically examine revered authorities in your own tradition? What do you fear losing if you find a flaw in something you've been taught? Pray for the courage to seek truth above all.

Second Objection: The Memory Argument and Induction
Al-Razi presents the second objection and begins his response, cutting off mid-sentence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second objection to the proof of the soul's non-eternity, which attacks the memory argument as weak induction, and see al-Razi's initial response that memory depends on the body.

Core Idea
Memory argument relies on weak induction; memory may depend on the body.

The second objection targets the argument that if souls were eternal, we would remember past states. Al-Razi dismisses this as clinging to induction (istiqra'), which is a weak method of reasoning. He suggests that memory of past states might be conditioned on attachment to the body with which the soul originated, but the text cuts off before the full refutation is given.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note how the objection is presented concisely and how al-Razi responds by calling it weak induction.
The response is incomplete; the text ends mid-sentence.
2
Understand the induction objection
Al-Razi claims that the memory argument is based on induction (istiqra'), which only yields probability, not certainty. This is a standard kalam critique of empirical reasoning.
Induction is considered weak because it cannot guarantee universal conclusions.
3
Consider the possible completion
The response begins to say that memory may depend on the specific body. Think about how this would refute the objection: if the soul had a previous body with different experiences, it might not remember them after changing bodies.
The cut-off makes this lesson a partial view; review the full refutation in other sources if needed.

Seventh and Eighth Objections: Celestial and Astrological Causes
Imam al-Razi presents two objections that miracles may originate from celestial or astrological forces.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how two objections from celestial and astrological causes challenge the certainty that miracles are from God.

Core Idea
Even doubtful possibilities can undermine certainty about miracles.

Imam al-Razi continues his series of objections, now turning to philosophical and astrological explanations for miracles. These objections do not claim that such explanations are true, but that their mere possibility prevents us from being certain that miracles come directly from God. This passage presents the seventh and eighth of eight total aspects.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the structure: two numbered objections followed by a conclusion.
2
Understand the seventh objection
Identify the philosophers' view on celestial beings. The objection argues that miracles could be attributed to these beings rather than God.
The objection does not affirm the philosophers' view; it merely points out the logical possibility.
3
Understand the eighth objection
Identify the astrologers' claims about the 'arrow of fortune' and 'arrow of the unseen'. The objection argues that if these claims were possible, miracles could be explained by astrology.
Imam al-Razi explicitly states that we know these claims are false, but the logical possibility remains.
4
Analyze the conclusion
Read the concluding sentence: it asserts that because of these eight objections, we cannot be certain that miracles are from God. Note that this is a challenge to certainty, not a denial of divine agency.
The conclusion ties back to the overall argument of the section.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه السابع : أن الفلاسفة يثبتون للأفلاك والكواكب عقولاً مجردة، ونفوسا ناطقة ونفوسا حيوانية فلكية فلم لا يجوز أن يكون المظهر لهذه الخوارق شيئًا من هذه الأشياء عقلا أو نفسا؟ الوجه الثامن : المنجمون اتفقوا على أن لسهم السعادة أثرا قويًا في تقوية الإنسان على تحصيل المرادات ،والسعادات ولسهم الغيب أثرًا قويًا في كون الإنسان متمكنا من الإخبار عن المغيبات، ونحن وإن كنا نعلم بالدليل عدم صدقهم في هذه المقالة إلا أن الاحتمال قائم وبتقدير أن يكون ما قالوه حقا لم يمكننا أن نقطع بأن ظهور المعجزات [من] الله تعالى ولا بأن نقطع بأن إخبار الأنبياء عن المغيبات بوحي الله تعالى، بل جاز أن يكون بقوة هذين السهمين في طوالعهم. فثبت بهذه الوجوه الثمانية أنه لا يمكن القطع بأن فاعل هذه المعجزات هو الله تعالى.
The seventh aspect: that the philosophers affirm for the spheres and planets abstract intellects, rational souls, and animal-astral souls. So why is it not permissible that the manifester of these extraordinary events be something from these things, either an intellect or a soul? The eighth aspect: The astrologers agree that the arrow of fortune has a strong effect in strengthening a person to obtain desired outcomes and felicities, and the arrow of the unseen has a strong effect in making a person capable of informing about hidden things. And even though we know by evidence their falsehood in this statement, nevertheless the possibility stands. And assuming that what they said is true, we cannot be certain that the appearance of miracles [is from] God, nor can we be certain that the prophets' informing about hidden things is by God's revelation, but rather it is possible that it is by the power of these two arrows in their ascendants. So it is established by these eight aspects that it is not possible to be certain that the agent of these miracles is God Almighty.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh and eighth aspects of a series of objections aimed at showing that we cannot be certain that miracles are performed by God. The seventh objection: If philosophers attribute miraculous phenomena to celestial intellects and souls, then there is no need to conclude that God is the direct agent; perhaps the miracle is the work of a celestial being. The eighth objection: Astrologers claim that certain astrological forces (the 'arrow of fortune' and the 'arrow of the unseen') can empower individuals to achieve extraordinary things or know the unseen. Even though believers know astrological claims to be false, the mere logical possibility that such forces could be responsible prevents us from being certain that a miracle is from God. The passage concludes that through these eight aspects (the last two of which are given here) we cannot be certain that the agent of miracles is God.

النفوس الحيوانية الفلكية
سهم السعادة

المنجمون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objections assume that the philosophical or astrological claims are true.
Correction: The objections are based on logical possibility, not on accepting those claims as true. Imam al-Razi explicitly says 'we know by evidence their falsehood'.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the seventh objection?
A) Miracles cannot occur at all.
B) Miracles might be caused by celestial intellects or souls, not necessarily by God.
C) Astrologers have proven that miracles are natural.
D) Philosophers deny the existence of miracles.

Key Takeaway
The mere possibility that miracles could originate from celestial or astrological sources undermines certainty that they are from God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience something you consider a miracle or answered prayer, do you ever entertain the possibility that it might have a natural or other explanation? How does that thought affect your certainty that Allah is directly involved?
?
Al-Razi argues that even false alternatives can prevent certainty. Is your faith in Allah's power and uniqueness shaken by the mere possibility of other causes? If not, what foundation grounds your certainty beyond witnessing miracles?
?
If you were challenged by a philosopher or astrologer claiming that your 'miracle' could have a non-divine origin, would you be able to maintain your certainty? What would you need to be absolutely sure it is from Allah?

Sixth Proof: Taklif Distracts from God and Its Conclusion
Sixth proof and conclusion of the first doubt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sixth argument against taklif and how its invalidity implies the invalidity of prophethood.

Core Idea
Taklif preoccupies the heart, hindering the highest goal of knowing and loving God.

Imam Razi continues presenting the doubts against taklif. The sixth proof argues that religious obligations necessarily preoccupy the heart, diverting it from the supreme purpose of creation: immersing in knowledge and love of Allah. If anything prevents this, it must be abandoned. The lesson then shows how this conclusion invalidates prophethood itself.

Guided Path
1
Read the Sixth Proof
Read the Arabic and translation of the sixth proof argument. Notice how it links preoccupation with prevention of immersion in knowledge and love of God.
The argument is concise; pay attention to the logical connectors.
2
Grasp the Logical Chain
Follow the reasoning: taklif necessitates preoccupation, preoccupation prevents immersion in knowledge and love of God, anything that prevents that is among the most obligatory duties to abandon, so taklif must be abandoned.
This is a conditional chain leading to a normative conclusion.
3
See the Broader Conclusion
Understand how the invalidity of taklif implies the invalidity of prophethood, since prophethood serves only to impose taklif.
The principle: if the purpose is invalid, the subordinate is more worthy of invalidity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السادس : أن التكليف يقتضي شغل القلب بتلك الأعمال، واشتغال القلب بغير يمنعه عن الاستغراق في معرفة الله ومحبته، وكل ما كان مانعا من المعرفة والمحبة كان تركه من أوجب الواجبات. فثبت بهذه الوجوه الستة أن القول بالتكليف باطل، وإذا ثبت هذا كان القول بالبعثة أيضًا باطلاً؛ لأنه لا فائدة من البعثة إلا توجيه التكاليف على الخلق، وإذا كان المقصود باطلا كان التبع أولى بالبطلان.
The sixth: that taklif necessitates preoccupying the heart with those acts, and preoccupation of the heart with other than Him prevents it from immersion in knowledge of God and love of Him. And everything that is a barrier to knowledge and love, abandoning it is among the most obligatory of duties. So it is established by these six proofs that the statement of taklif is invalid. And when this is established, the statement of prophethood (al-biʿtha) is also invalid, because there is no benefit from prophethood except directing obligations (takālīf) upon creation. And when the purpose is invalid, the subordinate is more worthy of invalidity.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This lesson presents the sixth proof and the conclusion of the first doubt. The sixth proof argues that taklif requires occupying the heart with acts of obedience, which distracts from the primary goal of immersion in God's knowledge and love. Anything that hinders knowledge and love of God should be abandoned as among the most obligatory duties. Therefore taklif should be abandoned. After listing all six proofs, they conclude that taklif is invalid, and since the only purpose of prophethood is to convey taklif, prophethood is also invalid. This completes the first doubt.

Key Terms
شغل القلب
استغراق
معرفة الله
محبة الله
بعثة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that taklif necessarily distracts from God and cannot be beneficial.
Correction: This argument assumes a dichotomy, but acts of worship can also enhance devotion and love of God, serving as means to the goal rather than barriers.

Checkpoint
According to the sixth proof, why should taklif be abandoned?
A) It is impossible to fulfill
B) It has no benefit
C) It distracts from knowledge and love of God
D) It leads to ignorance

Key Takeaway
Taklif is deemed invalid because it diverts from the ultimate goal of knowing and loving God, and prophethood, being its instrument, is also invalid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Can you identify a religious obligation or practice in your life that has become a mere routine, occupying your heart and mind but not drawing you closer to God? What would it take to strip it back to its spiritual essence or even set it aside if it truly blocks deeper intimacy?
?
If you were to honestly assess your daily worship, how much of it is performed out of habit or duty versus out of longing for knowledge and love of your Creator? What specific change can you make tomorrow to ensure your acts of worship are not distractions but bridges to immersion in Him?
?
The author argues that anything that prevents knowledge and love of God must be abandoned. Is there a practice, even one considered pious, that you cling to out of fear or tradition rather than because it brings you closer to Allah? Are you brave enough to examine it and, if needed, let it go for the sake of the ultimate goal?

Second Doubt: Knowledge of Good and Evil
Imam Razi enumerates three categories of moral knowledge and draws consequences for the need for prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the structure of the second doubt against prophethood and how it poses a dilemma about moral knowledge and the need for revelation.

Core Idea
If good and evil are self-evident, prophets are redundant; if not, obligation becomes unjust.

Imam Razi presents the second doubt of the deniers of prophethood. The challenge is that either we already know good and evil, making prophets unnecessary, or we do not know, in which case any obligation seems either compelled or unjust. This passage lays out the logical categories that frame this dilemma.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify three categories
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Identify the three categories of moral knowledge presented: known good, known evil, and unknown.
The author uses a conditional structure: 'if... then...'
2
Understand the implications of each category
For known good and known evil, there is no need for Sharia. For unknown, the passage splits into compelled vs. not compelled. Compelled actions (like breathing) would make obligation unjust.
The passage cuts off, so the implication for non-compelled actions is not fully stated.
3
Reflect on the dilemma
Ask yourself: How does this argument aim to cast doubt on the necessity of prophets? What assumption does it make about moral knowledge?
The deniers assume moral knowledge is either self-evident or cannot be obligated without injustice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والشبهة الثانية لمنكري النبوات أن الأفعال إما أن يكون حسنها معلوما، أو يكون قبحها معلوما ، أو لا نعلم لا حسنها ولا قبحها، فإن كان حسنها معلومًا عملناه، ولا حاجة بنا في ذلك إلى تعريف الشرع، وإن كان قبحها معلوما تركناه، وإن لم نعلم لا حسنها ولا قبحها فهذا الشيء إما أن يكون فعله اضطراريًا كالتنفس في الهواء، وما يجري مجراه وإما أن لا يكون كذلك، فإن كان فعله اضطراريًا كان جورًا لا محالة،
And the second doubt of the deniers of prophethood: that actions either have their goodness known, or their evil known, or we know neither their goodness nor their evil. If their goodness is known, we do it, and we have no need in that for the definition of the Sharia. And if their evil is known, we abandon it. And if we know neither their goodness nor their evil, then this thing: either its performance is compelled (iḍṭirārī), like breathing in the air and what is analogous to it, or it is not so. If its performance is compelled, then it is injustice (jawr) without doubt...
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage begins the second doubt (shubha) of the deniers of prophethood. The argument is that actions fall into three categories regarding moral knowledge. (1) If we know an action is good, we do it—no need for prophets to inform us. (2) If we know it is evil, we avoid it—again no need. (3) If we do not know its moral status, then either the action is compelled (like breathing) or not. If it is compelled, then commanding or forbidding it would be unjust because there is no choice. The argument is incomplete in this window, but it sets up a dilemma: if we already know good and evil, prophets are unnecessary; if we don't, we cannot be obligated because either the act is outside our control (compulsion) or, by implication, requires prophetic guidance, but the deniers presumably argue that such guidance is unreliable. The passage cuts off, but the direction is clear.

Key Terms
حسن (ḥusn)
قبح (qubḥ)
اضطراري (iḍṭirārī)
جور (jawr)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument assumes that all moral knowledge is self-evident or can be known without revelation, ignoring that many actions require revelation to know their true moral status or reward/punishment.
Correction: Ash'ari theology holds that good and evil are known primarily through revelation, not reason alone. Some actions may have rationally apparent moral qualities, but ultimate reward and punishment depend on divine command.

Checkpoint
According to the second doubt, if we know an action is good, what follows?
A) We need a prophet to confirm it
B) We perform it without needing Sharia
C) We are compelled to do it
D) It is unjust to command it

Key Takeaway
The second doubt challenges prophethood by arguing that if good and evil are known, prophets are unnecessary; if unknown, obligation becomes either compelled (unjust) or reliant on the very revelation it questions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever made a moral decision based solely on your own intuition, without consulting the Qur'an or Sunnah? How does this passage expose the danger of relying on your own sense of good and evil, and what will you do to ensure revelation guides your choices?
?
If someone were to argue that prophets are unnecessary because we already know right from wrong, would your own practice of Islam truly demonstrate the opposite? In what specific areas of your life do you actively seek prophetic guidance rather than trusting your own judgment?
?
The doubt claims that if an action's moral status is unknown and it is not compelled, then obligation becomes problematic. This forces you to ask: Do you truly believe that revelation is the only source of obligation? Or do you sometimes act as if your own reasoning can impose duties on yourself or others? Answer honestly and commit to seeking divine guidance before making moral judgments.

Ten Arguments Against Angelic Infallibility
Enumeration of ten objections against angelic infallibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ten arguments used by opponents of angelic infallibility, each derived from the angels' words and actions in the Quran.

Core Idea
The ten objections are drawn from the angels' own statements and behaviors in the Quran.

Imam al-Razi enumerates ten arguments raised by those who deny the infallibility (isma) of angels. These arguments are based on the story of Adam's creation and the angels' responses. Understanding these objections is essential for grasping the theological debate surrounding angelic infallibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of ten arguments
Start by reading through all ten arguments in the Arabic text and translation. Notice that each argument is numbered and derives from a specific Quranic verse or report.
The arguments are presented as a series of objections, not as the author's own view.
2
Identify the sin charged in each argument
For each argument, identify what sin the angels are accused of (e.g., objection, backbiting, conjecture, self-admiration, delusion). This helps in seeing the pattern of accusations.
3
Note the scriptural basis
Each argument is anchored in a Quranic verse. Pay attention to how the opponents interpret these verses to support their case.
The verses include 2:30-33, 53:28, 17:36, 37:165-166.
4
Reflect on the coherence of the objections
Consider whether these arguments form a consistent case against angelic infallibility. Notice that they range from overt actions to inner states like arrogance.
5
Prepare for the author's response
After understanding the arguments, anticipate how an advocate of angelic infallibility might respond. This sets the stage for the next lesson on the author's reply.
The author's response is brief but hinges on the distinction between clear and ambiguous texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقد احتجوا بها من عشرة أوجه:
:أحدها: أن قوله : أَتَجْعَلُ ؟ اعتراض والاعتراض على الله من أعظم الذنوب. وثانيها : أنهم طعنوا في بني آدم وهذا الطعن غيبة والغيبة من الذنوب
وثالثها : حكمهم على البشر بالفساد والقتل، ولا يجوز أن يقال: إنهم عرفوا بالوحي ؛ لأنه تعالى لما أراد إعزاز آدم وأولاده فكيف يليق بذلك اطلاع الأعداء على الغيوب؟ فثبت أنهم قالوا ذلك عن الظن والحسبان، وذلك عظيم لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنَّ الظَّنَّ لَا يُغْنِي مِنَ الْحَقِّ شَيْئًا [النجم: ۲۸] وقوله: ﴿وَلا تقف ما ليس لك به علم﴾ [الإسراء : ٣٦] .
ورابعها : أنهم لما طعنوا في بني آدم مدحوا أنفسهم فقالوا : ﴿وَنَحْنُ نُسَبِّحُ بِحَمْدِكَ وَنُقَدِّسُ لَكَ ﴾ [البَقَرَة : ٣٠] وقالوا : وَإِنَّا لَنَحْنُ الصَّافُونَ وَإِنَّا لَنَحْنُ الْمُسَبِّحُونَ [الصافات: ١٦٥ - ١٦٦] وهذا لفظ يدل على أنهم كانوا يقولون نحن الموصوفون بهذا التسبيح لا غيرنا وكل ذلك عجب والعجب من معظمات الذنوب، لقوله ﷺ «ثلاث مهلكات» إلى قوله : «وإعجاب المرء بنفسه».
وخامسها : أنهم ذكروا عن أنفسهم الطاعة، وما ذكروا أن ذلك حصل بتوفيق الله تعالى وإعانته، وهذا غرور، وهو من الذنوب. وسادسها : أنه تعالى قال لهم : ﴿لَوْ أَنْبِتُونِي بِأَسْمَاءِ هَؤُلَاءِ إِنْ كُنْتُمْ صَادِقِينَ﴾ [البقرة: ٣١] فهذا يدل على أنهم قد ذكروا كلاما وكانوا كاذبين فيه. وسابعها : قوله تعالى حكاية عنهم : ﴿قَالُوا سُبْحَنَكَ لَا عِلْمَ لَنَا إِلَّا مَا عَلَّمْتَنَا﴾ [البقرة : ٣٢] وهذا الكلام لا شك في أنه اعتذار، ولولا تقد الجرم وإلا لما احتاجوا إلى هذا الاعتذار.
وثامنها : قوله تعالى للملائكة : ﴿قَالَ أَلَمْ أَقُلْ لَكُمْ إِنِّي أَعْلَمُ غَيْبَ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ﴾ [البقرة: الآية ٣٣] وهذا الكلام يدل على أنهم كانوا شاكين في كونه تعالى عالما بجميع المعلومات.
وتاسعها : قوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَعْلَمُ مَا تُبْدُونَ وَمَا كُنْتُمْ تَكْتُمُونَ﴾ [البَقَرَة : ٣٣] وهذا يدل على أنهم فعلوا فعلا كانوا يكتمونه، وذلك يقتضي كونه ذنبا إذ لو كان طاعة لما احتاجوا إلى كتمانه.
وعاشرها يروى عن ابن عباس أنه قال: إن الله تعالى أمر إبليس مع عسكره بمحاربة الجان، ثم لما قال بعد ذلك : ﴿إِنِّي جَاعِلٌ فِي الْأَرْضِ خَلِيفَةً﴾ [البَقَرَة : ٣٠] قالوا ليخلق ربنا أي شيء شاء فلن يخلق ربنا خلقا أفضل منا، وهذا هو المراد من قوله : ﴿وَأَعْلَمُ مَا تُبْدُونَ وَمَا كُنْتُمْ تَكْتُمُونَ﴾ [البَقَرَة : ٣٣] وهذا يدل على أنهم وصفوا الله تعالى بأنه لا يقدر على خلق قوم أفضل منهم، ويدل ذلك على غاية الغرور والعجب، وكل ذلك من الذنوب الكبيرة.
فهذا شرح وجوه الاستدلال ممن ينكر عصمة الملائكة بهذه الآية. والجواب : أن الآيات التي تمسكنا بها في عصمة الملائكة صريحة في المقصود، وهذه الوجوه التي ذكرتموها محتملة والمحتمل لا يعارض الصريح. وأما الأجوبة المفصلة عن هذه الوجوه، فهي مذكورة في "كتاب التفسير".
Then they argued by it from ten aspects: First: that His statement 'Will You place...' is an objection, and objecting to Allah is among the greatest sins. Second: that they disparaged the children of Adam, and this disparagement is backbiting, and backbiting is among the sins. Third: they judged humankind with corruption and killing, and it cannot be said that they knew by revelation; because when He intended to honor Adam and his children, how would it be fitting that enemies be informed of the unseen? So it is established that they said that based on conjecture and assumption, and that is grave due to His statement 'And indeed, conjecture does not avail against the truth at all' (53:28) and His statement 'And do not pursue that of which you have no knowledge' (17:36). Fourth: when they disparaged the children of Adam, they praised themselves, saying 'while we exalt You with praise and sanctify You' (2:30) and they said 'Indeed, we are the ones who line up in ranks, and indeed we are the ones who exalt [Allah]' (37:165-166). This wording indicates that they were saying 'we are described with this exaltation, not others', and all of that is self-admiration, and self-admiration is among the major sins, due to his statement (the Prophet) 'three destroyers...' up to his statement 'and a person's self-admiration'. Fifth: they mentioned about themselves obedience, and they did not mention that this occurred through the success and assistance of Allah Almighty, and this is delusion, and it is among the sins. Sixth: He Almighty said to them: 'Inform Me of the names of these, if you are truthful' (2:31). This indicates that they had said something and were false in it. Seventh: His statement, narrating from them: 'They said, "Exalted are You; we have no knowledge except what You have taught us"' (2:32). This speech is undoubtedly an apology, and had there not been prior guilt, they would not have needed this apology. Eighth: His statement to the angels: 'He said, "Did I not tell you that I know the unseen of the heavens and the earth?"' (2:33). This speech indicates that they were doubtful about Him Almighty being knowledgeable of all things. Ninth: His statement: 'And I know what you reveal and what you have concealed' (2:33). This indicates that they did an act that they were concealing, and that necessitates it being a sin, because if it were obedience, they would not need to conceal it. Tenth: It is narrated from Ibn Abbas that he said: Allah Almighty commanded Iblis with his army to fight the jinn. Then when He later said: 'Indeed, I will make upon the earth a successive authority' (2:30), they said: 'Let our Lord create whatever He wills, our Lord will not create a creation better than us.' This is what is meant by His statement: 'And I know what you reveal and what you have concealed.' This indicates that they described Allah Almighty as being unable to create a people better than them, and that indicates extreme delusion and self-admiration, and all of that is from the major sins. So this is an explanation of the aspects of inference from those who deny the infallibility of the angels by this verse. And the answer: the verses we have adhered to regarding the infallibility of the angels are clear in their intent, and these aspects you have mentioned are ambiguous, and the ambiguous does not oppose the clear. As for the detailed answers to these aspects, they are mentioned in the Book of Tafsir.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage presents ten arguments used by those who deny the infallibility (isma) of angels, drawn from the story of the angels' question to Allah about the creation of Adam. The author, Imam al-Razi, then gives a brief response. The passage begins by stating that the opponents have argued using ten aspects from the verse. The first argument is that the angels' question 'Will You place...' is an objection, and objecting to Allah is a great sin. The second is that they disparaged humanity, which is backbiting. The third is that they judged humans as corrupt and violent without divine knowledge, relying on conjecture. The fourth is that they praised themselves while criticizing humans, which is self-admiration, considered a major sin. The fifth is that they attributed their obedience to themselves without acknowledging Allah's grace, which is delusion. The sixth is that Allah challenged them to inform Him of the names of things, showing they were mistaken. The seventh is that they apologized by saying 'we have no knowledge except what You taught us', implying prior fault. The eighth is that Allah's rebuke 'Did I not tell you...' shows they doubted His knowledge. The ninth is that Allah's knowledge of what they conceal indicates they had hidden something sinful. The tenth, from Ibn Abbas, states that the angels objected based on their superiority over humans, implying Allah could not create better, which is extreme arrogance. After listing these, the author summarizes that this is the argument of those denying angelic infallibility. Then he gives a concise response: the verses supporting angelic infallibility are clear (sarih), while these arguments are merely ambiguous (muhtamal), and the ambiguous cannot oppose the clear. He refers the reader to his Tafsir for detailed refutations.

Key Terms
اعتراض
غيبة
ظن
إعجاب
غرور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The ten arguments are Imam al-Razi's own position against angelic infallibility.
Correction: Imam al-Razi is presenting the arguments of his opponents to refute them. He affirms angelic infallibility and responds to these objections.

Checkpoint
According to the first argument, what is the sin attributed to the angels regarding their question 'Will You place...'?
A) It shows ignorance of Allah's plan
B) It is an objection to Allah, which is a great sin
C) It is a request for clarification, which is permissible
D) It is a test of Allah's wisdom

Key Takeaway
The ten objections against angelic infallibility are all drawn from the angels' own words and actions in the Quran, each accusing them of a specific sin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of the ten sins attributed to the angels (objection, backbiting, conjecture, self-admiration, delusion, falsehood, concealment, doubt, arrogance) do you see most clearly in your own heart right now? Name it, and then pray one sincere dua to Allah for forgiveness and protection from it.
?
The angels concealed a sin (argument 9). Is there a sin you are hiding from others or from yourself because you are ashamed to admit it? What would it look like to confess it to Allah and, if needed, to a trusted person, so that you can be free from its burden?
?
The angels thought Allah could not create better than them (argument 10). In what area of your life—your work, family, skills, or status—do you secretly believe you are irreplaceable or that no one else could do better? How can you deliberately humble yourself and affirm that Allah can raise up others beyond you?

The Author's Response: Clear vs Ambiguous
Brief response to the ten arguments, establishing the sarih-muhtamal principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam al-Razi's concise refutation of the ten arguments and the key principle that clear texts (sarih) take precedence over ambiguous ones (muhtamal).

Core Idea
The ambiguous does not oppose the clear — a fundamental principle in Quranic interpretation.

After presenting ten arguments against angelic infallibility, Imam al-Razi gives a brief but powerful response. He distinguishes between the verses that clearly support angelic infallibility and the ambiguous interpretations offered by the opponents. He then refers to his detailed commentary for a full refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the response passage
Read the Arabic text and translation of the response. Notice how short it is compared to the lengthy list of arguments.
The response is only a few lines, yet it establishes a key hermeneutical principle.
2
Understand the distinction between sarih and muhtamal
The author states that the verses supporting angelic infallibility are 'sarih' (clear, unequivocal) while the objections are 'muhtamal' (ambiguous, open to interpretation). This is a technical distinction in usul al-fiqh and kalam.
Sarih texts require no interpretation; muhtamal texts can bear multiple meanings.
3
Grasp the logical rule: al-muhtamal la yu'aridu al-sarih
The principle that an ambiguous text cannot oppose a clear text is crucial. When two texts seem contradictory, the clear one takes precedence, and the ambiguous one must be interpreted in light of the clear one.
This preserves the coherence of revelation.
4
Note the reference to Tafsir
The author mentions that detailed answers are in his 'Kitab al-Tafsir'. This shows that he has a comprehensive refutation, but here he only outlines the principle.
This also indicates the interconnectedness of his works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقد احتجوا بها من عشرة أوجه:
:أحدها: أن قوله : أَتَجْعَلُ ؟ اعتراض والاعتراض على الله من أعظم الذنوب. وثانيها : أنهم طعنوا في بني آدم وهذا الطعن غيبة والغيبة من الذنوب
وثالثها : حكمهم على البشر بالفساد والقتل، ولا يجوز أن يقال: إنهم عرفوا بالوحي ؛ لأنه تعالى لما أراد إعزاز آدم وأولاده فكيف يليق بذلك اطلاع الأعداء على الغيوب؟ فثبت أنهم قالوا ذلك عن الظن والحسبان، وذلك عظيم لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنَّ الظَّنَّ لَا يُغْنِي مِنَ الْحَقِّ شَيْئًا [النجم: ۲۸] وقوله: ﴿وَلا تقف ما ليس لك به علم﴾ [الإسراء : ٣٦] .
ورابعها : أنهم لما طعنوا في بني آدم مدحوا أنفسهم فقالوا : ﴿وَنَحْنُ نُسَبِّحُ بِحَمْدِكَ وَنُقَدِّسُ لَكَ ﴾ [البَقَرَة : ٣٠] وقالوا : وَإِنَّا لَنَحْنُ الصَّافُونَ وَإِنَّا لَنَحْنُ الْمُسَبِّحُونَ [الصافات: ١٦٥ - ١٦٦] وهذا لفظ يدل على أنهم كانوا يقولون نحن الموصوفون بهذا التسبيح لا غيرنا وكل ذلك عجب والعجب من معظمات الذنوب، لقوله ﷺ «ثلاث مهلكات» إلى قوله : «وإعجاب المرء بنفسه».
وخامسها : أنهم ذكروا عن أنفسهم الطاعة، وما ذكروا أن ذلك حصل بتوفيق الله تعالى وإعانته، وهذا غرور، وهو من الذنوب. وسادسها : أنه تعالى قال لهم : ﴿لَوْ أَنْبِتُونِي بِأَسْمَاءِ هَؤُلَاءِ إِنْ كُنْتُمْ صَادِقِينَ﴾ [البقرة: ٣١] فهذا يدل على أنهم قد ذكروا كلاما وكانوا كاذبين فيه. وسابعها : قوله تعالى حكاية عنهم : ﴿قَالُوا سُبْحَنَكَ لَا عِلْمَ لَنَا إِلَّا مَا عَلَّمْتَنَا﴾ [البقرة : ٣٢] وهذا الكلام لا شك في أنه اعتذار، ولولا تقد الجرم وإلا لما احتاجوا إلى هذا الاعتذار.
وثامنها : قوله تعالى للملائكة : ﴿قَالَ أَلَمْ أَقُلْ لَكُمْ إِنِّي أَعْلَمُ غَيْبَ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ﴾ [البقرة: الآية ٣٣] وهذا الكلام يدل على أنهم كانوا شاكين في كونه تعالى عالما بجميع المعلومات.
وتاسعها : قوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَعْلَمُ مَا تُبْدُونَ وَمَا كُنْتُمْ تَكْتُمُونَ﴾ [البَقَرَة : ٣٣] وهذا يدل على أنهم فعلوا فعلا كانوا يكتمونه، وذلك يقتضي كونه ذنبا إذ لو كان طاعة لما احتاجوا إلى كتمانه.
وعاشرها يروى عن ابن عباس أنه قال: إن الله تعالى أمر إبليس مع عسكره بمحاربة الجان، ثم لما قال بعد ذلك : ﴿إِنِّي جَاعِلٌ فِي الْأَرْضِ خَلِيفَةً﴾ [البَقَرَة : ٣٠] قالوا ليخلق ربنا أي شيء شاء فلن يخلق ربنا خلقا أفضل منا، وهذا هو المراد من قوله : ﴿وَأَعْلَمُ مَا تُبْدُونَ وَمَا كُنْتُمْ تَكْتُمُونَ﴾ [البَقَرَة : ٣٣] وهذا يدل على أنهم وصفوا الله تعالى بأنه لا يقدر على خلق قوم أفضل منهم، ويدل ذلك على غاية الغرور والعجب، وكل ذلك من الذنوب الكبيرة.
فهذا شرح وجوه الاستدلال ممن ينكر عصمة الملائكة بهذه الآية. والجواب : أن الآيات التي تمسكنا بها في عصمة الملائكة صريحة في المقصود، وهذه الوجوه التي ذكرتموها محتملة والمحتمل لا يعارض الصريح. وأما الأجوبة المفصلة عن هذه الوجوه، فهي مذكورة في "كتاب التفسير".
Then they argued by it from ten aspects: First: that His statement 'Will You place...' is an objection, and objecting to Allah is among the greatest sins. Second: that they disparaged the children of Adam, and this disparagement is backbiting, and backbiting is among the sins. Third: they judged humankind with corruption and killing, and it cannot be said that they knew by revelation; because when He intended to honor Adam and his children, how would it be fitting that enemies be informed of the unseen? So it is established that they said that based on conjecture and assumption, and that is grave due to His statement 'And indeed, conjecture does not avail against the truth at all' (53:28) and His statement 'And do not pursue that of which you have no knowledge' (17:36). Fourth: when they disparaged the children of Adam, they praised themselves, saying 'while we exalt You with praise and sanctify You' (2:30) and they said 'Indeed, we are the ones who line up in ranks, and indeed we are the ones who exalt [Allah]' (37:165-166). This wording indicates that they were saying 'we are described with this exaltation, not others', and all of that is self-admiration, and self-admiration is among the major sins, due to his statement (the Prophet) 'three destroyers...' up to his statement 'and a person's self-admiration'. Fifth: they mentioned about themselves obedience, and they did not mention that this occurred through the success and assistance of Allah Almighty, and this is delusion, and it is among the sins. Sixth: He Almighty said to them: 'Inform Me of the names of these, if you are truthful' (2:31). This indicates that they had said something and were false in it. Seventh: His statement, narrating from them: 'They said, "Exalted are You; we have no knowledge except what You have taught us"' (2:32). This speech is undoubtedly an apology, and had there not been prior guilt, they would not have needed this apology. Eighth: His statement to the angels: 'He said, "Did I not tell you that I know the unseen of the heavens and the earth?"' (2:33). This speech indicates that they were doubtful about Him Almighty being knowledgeable of all things. Ninth: His statement: 'And I know what you reveal and what you have concealed' (2:33). This indicates that they did an act that they were concealing, and that necessitates it being a sin, because if it were obedience, they would not need to conceal it. Tenth: It is narrated from Ibn Abbas that he said: Allah Almighty commanded Iblis with his army to fight the jinn. Then when He later said: 'Indeed, I will make upon the earth a successive authority' (2:30), they said: 'Let our Lord create whatever He wills, our Lord will not create a creation better than us.' This is what is meant by His statement: 'And I know what you reveal and what you have concealed.' This indicates that they described Allah Almighty as being unable to create a people better than them, and that indicates extreme delusion and self-admiration, and all of that is from the major sins. So this is an explanation of the aspects of inference from those who deny the infallibility of the angels by this verse. And the answer: the verses we have adhered to regarding the infallibility of the angels are clear in their intent, and these aspects you have mentioned are ambiguous, and the ambiguous does not oppose the clear. As for the detailed answers to these aspects, they are mentioned in the Book of Tafsir.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage presents ten arguments used by those who deny the infallibility (isma) of angels, drawn from the story of the angels' question to Allah about the creation of Adam. The author, Imam al-Razi, then gives a brief response. The passage begins by stating that the opponents have argued using ten aspects from the verse. The first argument is that the angels' question 'Will You place...' is an objection, and objecting to Allah is a great sin. The second is that they disparaged humanity, which is backbiting. The third is that they judged humans as corrupt and violent without divine knowledge, relying on conjecture. The fourth is that they praised themselves while criticizing humans, which is self-admiration, considered a major sin. The fifth is that they attributed their obedience to themselves without acknowledging Allah's grace, which is delusion. The sixth is that Allah challenged them to inform Him of the names of things, showing they were mistaken. The seventh is that they apologized by saying 'we have no knowledge except what You taught us', implying prior fault. The eighth is that Allah's rebuke 'Did I not tell you...' shows they doubted His knowledge. The ninth is that Allah's knowledge of what they conceal indicates they had hidden something sinful. The tenth, from Ibn Abbas, states that the angels objected based on their superiority over humans, implying Allah could not create better, which is extreme arrogance. After listing these, the author summarizes that this is the argument of those denying angelic infallibility. Then he gives a concise response: the verses supporting angelic infallibility are clear (sarih), while these arguments are merely ambiguous (muhtamal), and the ambiguous cannot oppose the clear. He refers the reader to his Tafsir for detailed refutations.

Key Terms
صريح
محتمل
عصمة الملائكة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Razi, what is the relationship between the verses supporting angelic infallibility and the ten arguments?
A) The verses are ambiguous while the arguments are clear
B) The verses are clear and the arguments are ambiguous, so the arguments do not contradict the verses
C) Both are equally clear, so they must be reconciled
D) The arguments are more authoritative than the verses

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Razi's response establishes that the clear verses affirming angelic infallibility take precedence over the ambiguous objections, a key principle in Quranic hermeneutics.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When a doubt about your faith arises, do you instinctively cling to the clear, unambiguous verses of the Quran, or do you let ambiguous interpretations unsettle you? Think of one specific doubt you have faced or are facing. What is the clear verse that directly addresses it, and will you write it down today to anchor your heart?
?
Imam al-Razi confidently states that the ambiguous cannot override the clear. In your life, are there areas where you allow unclear thoughts or desires to override what you know is true about Allah? What is one clear truth about His mercy or justice that you sometimes doubt? Will you commit to repeating that truth in your prayers this week until it settles in your heart?

Refuting the Claim that Iblis Was an Angel
Imam al-Razi refutes the claim that Iblis was an angel with three proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam al-Razi refutes the claim that Iblis was an angel and the three proofs he uses from the Quran and reason.

Core Idea
Iblis was not an angel; the Quran itself shows he was from the jinn.

Imam al-Razi addresses a common objection against angelic infallibility: the case of Iblis. Some argue that Iblis was an angel who fell into sin, but al-Razi provides clear evidence from the Quran that Iblis was from the jinn, not the angels. This lesson examines his refutation and the three proofs he presents.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and its reasons
Start by reading the objection that Iblis was an angel, along with the two reasons given for this claim. Notice how the objectors use the exception in the Quranic verses.
The exception 'except Iblis' is their main linguistic argument.
2
Examine al-Razi's first proof
Al-Razi denies the premise and gives his first proof: Iblis was from the jinn, as shown in Sura Saba where angels disavow worship and attribute it to jinn. This establishes jinn as a separate genus.
The verse clearly distinguishes between worship of angels and worship of jinn.
3
Analyze the second proof about progeny
The second proof: Iblis has progeny, mentioned in Sura al-Kahf. Angels have no progeny because they have no females, as stated in Sura al-Zukhruf.
Progeny requires male and female, which angels lack.
4
Consider the third proof about creation
The third proof: Iblis was created from fire, while angels are created from light. This difference in substance indicates they are different kinds of beings.
The narration from Aisha supports the idea that angels are created from light.
5
Reflect on the overall refutation
Understand how these three proofs collectively refute the claim that Iblis was an angel, thereby preserving the doctrine of angelic infallibility.
Each proof is independent but together they are conclusive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشبهة الثانية قالوا : إن إبليس كان من الملائكة ثم إنه صدر عنه الكفر والفسق، وإنما قلنا : إنه كان من الملائكة لوجهين :
الأول: قوله : فَسَجَدُوا إِلَّا إِبْلِيسَ [البَقَرَة : ٣٤] وقوله : فَسَجَدَ الْمَلَائِكَةُ كُلُّهُمْ أَجْمَعُونَ إِلَّا إِبْلِيسَ [الحجر: ۳۰ - ۳۱] والاستثناء لا يكون إلا من الجنس.
الثاني : أنه لو لم يكن من الملائكة لكان أمر الله للملائكة بالسجود غير متناول له، فوجب أن لا تحصل له صفة الذنب بترك السجود، فضلا عن الكفر.
والجواب عن الشبهة الثانية: لا نسلم أن إبليس كان من الملائكة، ويدل عليه وجوه :
الأول : أن إبليس كان من الجن والجن ليسوا من الملائكة لقوله تعالى : ﴿وَيَوْمَ يَحْشُرُهُمْ جَمِيعًا ثُمَّ يَقُولُ لِلْمَلَائِكَةِ أَهَؤُلَاءِ إِيَّاكُمْ كَانُوا يَعْبُدُونَ قَالُوا سُبْحَنَكَ أَنتَ وَلِيُّنَا مِن دُونِهِمْ بَلْ كَانُوا يَعْبُدُونَ الْجِنَّ﴾ [سبأ : ٤٠ - ٤١] دلت الآية على أنهم ما كانوا يعبدون الملائكة، بل كانوا يعبدون الجن، فوجب أن يكون جنسا غير الملائكة.
الثاني: أن إبليس له ذرية لقوله تعالى : ﴿أَفَتَتَّخِذُونَهُ وَذُرِّيَّتَهُ أَوْلِيَاءَ مِن دُونِي﴾ [الكهف: ٥٠] والملائكة لا ذرية لهم؛ لأن الذرية لا تكون إلا عند اجتماع الذكر والأنثى، وليس في الملائكة أنثى، لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَجَعَلُوا الْمَلَائِكَةَ الَّذِينَ هُمْ عِبَادُ الرَّحْمَنِ إِنَاثًا﴾ [الزخرف: ۱۹] .
الثالث : أن إبليس مخلوق من النار، قال الله تعالى حكاية عنه : ﴿خَلَقْتَنِي مِن نَّارٍ وَخَلَقْتَهُ مِن طِينٍ﴾ والملائكة مخلوقون من النور، ولما روى عروة عن عائشة عن
The second objection: They said, 'Iblis was from the angels, then disbelief and immorality proceeded from him. And we have said that he was from the angels for two reasons: First: His statement: "So they prostrated except Iblis" (2:34) and His statement: "So the angels prostrated, all of them together, except Iblis" (15:30-31). And the exception can only be from the genus. Second: If he were not from the angels, then Allah's command to the angels to prostrate would not have applied to him, so he would not have acquired the attribute of sin by abandoning prostration, let alone disbelief.' And the answer to the second objection: We do not accept that Iblis was from the angels, and there are proofs for this: First: Iblis was from the jinn, and the jinn are not from the angels, due to His statement: 'And on the Day when He will gather them all together, then He will say to the angels, "Was it you that these used to worship?" They will say, "Exalted are You; You are our Protector, not them. Rather, they used to worship the jinn"' (34:40-41). The verse indicates that they did not worship the angels, but rather they used to worship the jinn, so it is necessary that they are a genus other than the angels. Second: Iblis has progeny, due to His statement: 'Then will you take him and his progeny as allies instead of Me?' (18:50). And the angels have no progeny, because progeny only comes from the meeting of male and female, and there is no female among the angels, due to His statement: 'And they have made the angels, who are servants of the Most Merciful, females' (43:19). Third: Iblis was created from fire, Allah Almighty said narrating from him: 'You created me from fire and created him from clay' (7:12). And the angels were created from light, and as narrated by Urwa from Aisha from...
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage presents the second objection against angelic infallibility and its refutation. The objectors claim that Iblis was an angel and then fell into disbelief, thus proving that angels can sin. They give two reasons: first, the Quran excludes Iblis from the prostration of the angels, implying he was one of them (since exception is from the genus). Second, if he were not an angel, Allah's command to prostrate would not apply to him, so he would not be guilty. The author refutes this by denying that Iblis was an angel, offering three proofs. The first proof: Iblis was from the jinn, as indicated in Sura Saba (34:40-41) where the angels disavow worship and say that people worshipped jinn, not angels. Thus jinn are a separate genus. The second proof: Iblis has progeny (mentioned in Sura al-Kahf 18:50), whereas angels have no progeny because they have no females (Sura al-Zukhruf 43:19). The third proof (incomplete in this passage): Iblis was created from fire (Sura al-A'raf 7:12) while angels were created from light, with a supporting narration. Thus the objection is refuted.

ملائكة
جن
ذرية
خلق من نار
خلق من نور
استثناء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The exception 'except Iblis' in the prostration verses proves he was an angel.
Correction: Exception does not always indicate belonging to the same genus if there is contrary evidence. Al-Razi shows from other verses that Iblis was from the jinn, a separate creation.

Checkpoint
What is the first proof given by Imam al-Razi to refute the claim that Iblis was an angel?
A) Iblis was created from fire, not light
B) Iblis has progeny, while angels do not
C) The Quran states that Iblis was from the jinn, a separate genus from angels
D) Iblis was ordered to prostrate but refused

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Razi demonstrates that Iblis was not an angel but from the jinn, based on Quranic verses about worship, progeny, and creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson reveals that your greatest enemy, Iblis, is a jinn who chose disobedience. Knowing that he is not a fallen angel but a defiant jinn, how does this change the way you view his deception and your own accountability in resisting him today? Will you take one concrete step to guard against his whisperings before you sleep tonight?
?
The angels are perfectly obedient, yet you are not an angel. In which area of your life have you been acting as if obedience is optional, like Iblis, rather than essential, like the angels? What will you change today to align your actions with the worship that Allah deserves from His conscious servants?
?
The objectors in this passage relied on a grammatical assumption without checking the rest of the Quran. Is there a belief you hold about Allah or His creation that you have accepted without verifying against the Book? Will you commit to studying one Quranic passage this week to test that belief?

Razi’s Objections to Angelic Superiority from 4:172
Razi presents three objections and a verification on Quran 4:172 and angelic superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Razi critiques the argument that Quran 4:172 proves angelic superiority, using logical and linguistic analysis.

Core Idea
The verse proves power, not necessarily reward.

Imam al-Razi engages with those who use Quran 4:172 to argue that angels are superior to humans, specifically to the Messiah Jesus. He presents three objections and a detailed verification, showing that the verse only indicates superiority in power and might, not in reward. This lesson walks through his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the full Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Razi structures his objections and verification.
The passage uses technical terms like 'mubalaghah' and 'dawr'.
2
Identify the three objections
Razi presents three numbered objections: second (plural form), third (conjunction and example), fourth (partial superiority). Locate each and understand their core claim.
3
Examine the verification section
After the third objection, Razi provides a verification using the minister-sultan example. Understand how he identifies circular reasoning and moves to the fourth objection.
This section clarifies the intended meaning of the verse.
4
Understand the final conclusion
Razi accepts the verse as proof for superiority in power and might but rejects it for reward. He also offers an alternative interpretation about angels being more wondrous than Jesus.
This concludes his analysis of the verse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني : أن قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا الْمَلَائِكَةُ الْمُقَرَّبُونَ) [النساء: ۱۷۲] صيغة لجمع وصيغة الجمع تتناول الكل، وهذا يقتضي كون مجموع الملائكة أفضل من المسيح فلم قلتم إنه يقتضي كون كل واحد من الملائكة أفضل من المسيح ؟ والثالث: أن الواو في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا الْمَلَائِكَةُ المُقَرَّبُونَ) [النساء : ۱۷۲] حرف العطف، وهو يفيد الجمع المطابق، ولا يفيد الترتيب - على ما ذكرناه في أصول الفقه - وأما المثال الذي ذكرتموه فليس بحجة ؛ لأن الحكم الكلي لا يثبت بالمثال الجزئي، ثم إنه معارض بسائر الأمثلة كقولك : ما أعانني على هذا الأمر لا زيد ولا عمر، وهذا لا يفيد كون المتأخر في الذكر أفضل من المتقدم، ومنه قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا الْهدى ولا الْقَلَائِدَ ولا آمِّينَ الْبَيْتَ الْحَرَامَ﴾ [المائدة: ٢] ولما اختلفت الأمثلة امتنع التعويل عليها. ثم التحقيق في هذه المسألة أنه إذا قيل : هذا العالم لا يستنكف الوزير من خدمته ولا السلطان، فنحن نعلم بعقولنا أن السلطان أعظم درجة من الوزير، فعلمنا أن الغرض من ذكر الثاني هو المبالغة وهذه المبالغة إنما عرفناها بهذا الطريق لا بمجرد الترتيب في الذكر. وههنا في هذه الآية لا يمكننا أن نعرف أن المراد من قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا الْمَلَائِكَةُ المُقَرَّبُونَ﴾ [النساء : ۱۷۲] بيان المبالغة إلا إذا عرفنا قبل ذلك أن الملائكة المقربين أفضل من المسيح . وحينئذ يتوقف صحة الدليل على صحة المدلول، وذلك دور. الرابع : هب أن هذه الآية دالة على أن منصب الملك أعلى وأزيد من منصب المسيح، لكنها لا تدل على أن تلك الزيادة في جميع المناصب أو في بعضها ؛ فإنه إذا قيل هذا العالم لا يستنكف من خدمته الوزير ولا السلطان فهو لا يفيد إلا أن السلطان أكمل من الوزير في بعض الأشياء، وهي القدرة والسلطنة، ولا يفيد كون السلطان أزيد من الوزير في الزهد والعلم. إذا ثبت هذا فنحن نقول بموجبه ؛ وذلك لأن الملك أفضل من البشر في القدرة، والقوة والبطش ؛ فإن جبريل القلع مدائن لوط والبشر لا يقدرون على شيء من ذلك، فلم قلتم : إن الملك أفضل من البشر في كثرة الثواب الحاصل بسبب مزيد الخشوع والعبودية ؟ وتمام التحقيق : أن الفضل المختلف فيه في هذه المسألة هو كثرة الثواب، ثم إن كثرة الثواب لا تحصل إلا بنهاية التواضع والخضوع، وكون العبد موصوفا بنهاية التواضع لله تعالى لا يلائم صيرورته مستنكفًا عن عبودية الله تعالى، بل ينافيها ويناقضها، فامتنع أن يكون المراد من الآية هذا المعنى، أما اتصاف الشخص بالقدرة الشديدة والقوة الكاملة فإنه مناسب للتمرد وترك العبودية. والنصارى لما شاهدوا من المسيح إحياء الموتى وإبراء الأكمه والأبرص أخرجوه بسبب هذا القدر من القدرة عن عبودية الله تعالى فقال تعالى: (لَن يَسْتَكْفَ الْمَسِيحُ أن يكون عَبْدًا لِلَّهِ ﴾ [النساء : ۱۷۲] أي أن عيسى لن يستنكف بهذا القدر من القدرة عن عبوديتي ولا الملائكة المقربون الذين هم فوقه في القدرة والبطش والاستيلاء على عالم السماوات والأرضين. وبهذا الوجه تنتظم دلالة الآية على أن الملك أفضل من البشر في القدرة والبطش والشدة لكنها لا تدل البتة على أن الملك أفضل من البشر في كثرة الثواب . أو يقال : إنهم إنما ادعوا الهية المسيح لأنه حصل من غير أب فقيل لهم : الملائكة حصلوا لا من أب ولا أم، فكانوا أعجب من عيسى في هذا الباب مع أنهم لا يستنكفون عن عبودية الله تعالى.
The second (objection): that the saying of Allah Most High: 'nor the nearest angels' [4:172] is a plural form, and the plural form encompasses the whole, and this necessitates that the totality of angels is better than the Messiah. So why did you say that it necessitates that every single one of the angels is better than the Messiah? The third: that the waw in the saying of Allah Most High: 'nor the nearest angels' [4:172] is a conjunction, and it indicates pure aggregation, and does not indicate order – as we mentioned in Usul al-Fiqh. As for the example you mentioned, it is not a proof; because a universal ruling is not established by a particular example. Moreover, it is contradicted by other examples, like your saying: 'No Zayd nor Amr helped me in this matter' – this does not indicate that the later mentioned is better than the former. And from this is the saying of Allah Most High: 'nor the sacrificial animals, nor the garlands, nor those intending the Sacred House' [5:2]. Since the examples differ, reliance upon them is impermissible. Then the verification in this issue: that when it is said: 'This scholar is not too proud to serve him – neither the minister nor the sultan,' we know by our intellects that the sultan is greater in rank than the minister. So we know that the purpose of mentioning the second is exaggeration (mubalaghah). And this exaggeration is known by this method, not merely by order of mention. And here in this verse, we cannot know that the intended meaning of His saying 'nor the nearest angels' is an exaggeration unless we already know that the nearest angels are better than the Messiah. Then the validity of the proof depends on the validity of the conclusion, and that is a vicious circle (dawr). The fourth: Grant that this verse indicates that the station of the angel is higher and more than the station of the Messiah, yet it does not indicate whether that increase is in all stations or in some of them. For if it is said: 'This scholar is not too proud to serve him – neither the minister nor the sultan,' it indicates only that the sultan is more perfect than the minister in some things, namely power and authority, and does not indicate that the sultan exceeds the minister in asceticism and knowledge. If this is established, then we accept its implication; that is because the angel is better than humans in power, strength, and might – for Gabriel uprooted the cities of Lot, and humans are capable of none of that. So why do you say that the angel is better than humans in the abundance of reward (kathrat al-thawab) resulting from increased humility and worship? And the complete verification: that the merit disputed in this issue is abundance of reward. Then abundance of reward is not attained except by extreme humility and submission. A servant being characterized by extreme humility to Allah Most High is not compatible with his becoming disdainful of the worship of Allah; rather it contradicts and opposes it. So it is impossible that the intended meaning of the verse is this meaning. As for a person being characterized by extreme power and complete strength, that is suitable for rebellion and abandonment of worship. The Christians, when they witnessed from the Messiah the reviving of the dead and the healing of the blind and the leper, they removed him due to this amount of power from the worship of Allah Most High. So Allah Most High said: 'The Messiah will never disdain to be a servant of Allah' [4:172], meaning that Jesus will not disdain due to this amount of power from My worship, nor the nearest angels who are above him in power, might, and control over the worlds of the heavens and the earths. And in this way, the indication of the verse is consistent that the angel is better than humans in power, might, and severity, but it does not indicate at all that the angel is better than humans in abundance of reward. Or it may be said: They claimed the divinity of the Messiah because he was born without a father, so it was said to them: The angels were created without father or mother, so they are more wondrous than Jesus in this regard, yet they do not disdain the worship of Allah Most High.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive theological analysis by Imam al-Razi of the verse 'nor the nearest angels' (Quran 4:172), used by those who argue for the superiority of angels over humans (specifically over the Messiah, Jesus). The passage presents three objections to this argument, followed by a detailed verification. The first objection (الثاني) argues that the plural form 'الملائكة' indicates the totality of angels, not each individual, so it does not prove that every angel is better than Jesus. The second objection (الثالث) focuses on the conjunction 'wa' (و), stating it merely aggregates, not orders, so the later mention of angels does not imply they are better. It also criticizes relying on an example like 'neither the minister nor the sultan' because universal rules cannot be derived from a single example, and other examples like Quran 5:2 show inconsistency. Then comes the 'تحقيق' (verification), which analyzes the 'minister-sultan' example: we know by reason that the sultan is higher, so mentioning him second is for exaggeration (mubalaghah). But in the verse, we cannot know that the mention of angels is for exaggeration unless we already know they are better, leading to circular reasoning (دور). The third objection (الرابع) concedes the verse shows superiority in some aspects (power, authority) but not in all, especially not in asceticism, knowledge, or reward. Al-Razi then accepts the verse's implication: angels are better in power and might, citing Gabriel's destruction of Lot's cities. However, the disputed merit is 'abundance of reward' (كثرة الثواب), which requires extreme humility. Since power can lead to rebelliousness, but humility characterizes worship, the verse cannot prove superiority in reward. The passage concludes that the verse's consistent interpretation is that angels are superior in power but not necessarily in reward, and offers an alternative interpretation: angels are more wondrous than Jesus because they lack parents, yet they worship God without disdain.

Key Terms
الملائكة المقربون
المسيح
المبالغة
الدور
القدرة
البطش
كثرة الثواب
التواضع
العبودية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any mention of angels after humans in a verse implies angelic superiority in all aspects.
Correction: Razi shows that linguistic context and logical analysis reveal the verse only proves superiority in power and might, not in reward or other virtues.

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Razi's analysis, what does the verse 'nor the nearest angels' (4:172) actually prove regarding angelic superiority over humans?
A) That angels are superior in all aspects, including reward.
B) That angels are superior only in power and might, not necessarily in reward.
C) That humans are superior to angels because of their humility.
D) That the verse is ambiguous and cannot be used for any argument.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Razi demonstrates that the verse only shows angelic superiority in power, not in reward, and that the argument for superiority in reward is flawed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read Quranic verses, do you ever assume that the order of mention implies a rank? How can Razi's analysis of the conjunction 'wa' change the way you interpret the Quran? Will you now pause to consider if an argument is based on grammar rather than substance?
?
Razi shows that power and might (like that of Gabriel) do not necessarily indicate higher reward in the sight of Allah. Think about your own life: do you admire powerful people more than humble worshippers? Where does your heart truly place value? Ask Allah to grant you humility, which is the key to reward, not worldly power.
?
Razi argues that the verse could be interpreted to show angels are more wondrous than Jesus because they were created without father or mother, yet they worship God. Have you ever used a similar reasoning to defend your faith? Reflect on a time you argued for Islam: did you rely on reasoning from the Quran like Razi, or did you rely on feelings? Commit to using sound logical arguments grounded in revelation.

The Mu'tazilite Proof from Verse 4:14 and Razi's Response
Razi presents the first Mu'tazilite proof, its objection, and his contextual response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi refutes the Mu'tazilite proof that verse 4:14 threatens all sinners with eternal fire by interpreting 'limits' contextually as inheritance rules.

Core Idea
Context determines meaning: the 'limits' in the verse refer to inheritance, not all sins.

One of the most common Mu'tazilite proofs for the eternal punishment of grave sinners comes from Quran 4:14, which threatens eternal fire for those who disobey God and transgress His limits. In this passage, Razi presents the proof, then raises a sophisticated objection based on the generality of the word 'limits', and finally provides an Ash'ari response that anchors the meaning in the immediate context of inheritance laws. This lesson walks through each stage of the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazilite proof
Read the verse and the Mu'tazilite interpretation that transgression of limits includes all major sins. Notice how they assume 'limits' refers to all divine commands.
The Mu'tazila use this verse to argue that any major sin leads to eternal hell.
2
Consider the objection
The objection argues that 'limits' (ḥudūd) is a definite plural, implying that transgression of all limits is required. This is impossible for any single person, or only possible for a disbeliever.
This objection is based on the principle of 'umūm (generality) in Arabic linguistics.
3
Study Razi's response
Notice how Razi points to the preceding verses about inheritance to restrict the meaning of 'limits'. He shows that the same word was used earlier in the surah for inheritance rules, so the threat applies only to those who violate those specific rulings.
This is a classic Ash'ari move: interpreting ambiguous verses in light of context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الأولى : قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَن يَعْصِ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ وَيَتَعَدَّ حُدُودَهُ يُدْخِلْهُ نَارًا خَالِدًا فِيهَا﴾ [النساء : ١٤] ومعلوم أن من ترك الصلاة والحج والزكاة والصوم وقتل وزنى ولاط فقد تعدى الحدود.
فإن قيل : الحدود لفظ جمع دخل فيه حرف التعريف فيفيد العموم، وتعدي الحدود لا يصدق إلا عند تعدي جميع الحدود، وهو إما أن لا يكون ممكنا أو يكون ممكنا لكنه لا يثبت إلا في حق الكافر ، أما أنه غير ممكن فلأن من تعدى بالمجوسية ذلك أن يتعدى باليهودية ومن تعدى بالفعل لا يمكنه في تلك الحالة أن يتعدى بالترك.
وأيضًا: فإن كان ذلك ممكنا إلا أنه لا يتحقق إلا في حق الكافر، فكانت الآية مختصة بالكافر.
قلنا : إنه تعالى شرح حدود الميراث في مقدمة هذه الآية، ثم قال: ﴿وَتِلْكَ حُدُودُ اللَّهِ﴾ [البقرة : ١٨٧] فانصرف هذا الحد إلى الحدود المذكورة فيما تقدم، وهي حدود الميراث، ثم قال: ﴿وَمَن يَعْصِ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ وَيَتَعَدَّ حُدُودَهُ﴾ [النساء : ١٤] فقوله: ﴿وَيَتَعَدَّ حُدُودَهُ﴾ لا يبعد أن يكون منصرفًا إلى الحدود المذكورة فيما قبل ذلك، فثبت أن هذا الوعيد مختص بمن تعدى الحدود المذكورة في الميراث.
The first proof: His saying, exalted: {And whoever disobeys God and His messenger and transgresses His limits, He will admit him into a fire, abiding eternally therein} [al-Nisa: 14]. And it is known that whoever abandons prayer, pilgrimage, zakah, fasting, kills, commits adultery, and sodomy has transgressed the limits.
If it is said: "Limits" is a plural word with the definite article, so it indicates generality, and transgression of the limits is not true except by transgressing all limits. That is either impossible or possible but only established for the disbeliever. As for it being impossible, because one who transgresses by Magianism cannot also transgress by Judaism, and one who transgresses by action cannot at that same state transgress by omission. Also, if that is possible, it is only realized in the case of the disbeliever, so the verse is specific to the disbeliever.
We say: He, exalted, explained the limits of inheritance in the introduction to this verse, then said: {And those are the limits of God} [al-Baqara: 187], so this reference (to limits) is turned to the limits mentioned previously, which are the limits of inheritance. Then He said: {And whoever disobeys God and His messenger and transgresses His limits} [al-Nisa: 14]. So His saying: {and transgresses His limits} is not unlikely to be referring to the limits mentioned before that. Thus it is established that this threat is specific to whoever transgresses the limits mentioned in inheritance.
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage presents the first Mu'tazilite proof from the Quran, along with an objection (fa-in qīla) and a response (qulnā). The Mu'tazila cite verse 4:14 which threatens with eternal fire those who disobey God and His messenger and transgress His limits. They assume that 'limits' here refers to all divine commands, so anyone guilty of a major sin is threatened. The objection argues that the word 'limits' (ḥudūd) is a definite plural, implying that transgression of all limits is required for the threat to apply. But it is impossible for one person to transgress all limits (e.g., by both commission and omission, or by adopting multiple false religions). Even if possible, it only applies to a disbeliever, so the verse is about disbelievers, not believers who commit sins. Razi then gives the Ash'ari response: the limits referred to in the context are the specific limits of inheritance mentioned just before in the same surah. Therefore, the threat applies only to those who transgress inheritance laws, not to all sinners.

Key Terms
الحدود
العموم
الخصوص
الميراث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the objection is the Mu'tazilite position, but it is actually a critique of their proof, answered by Razi.
Correction: The objection is raised by an opponent of the Mu'tazilite proof, not by the Mu'tazilites themselves. Razi then provides the Ash'ari response to the objection.

Checkpoint
How does Razi respond to the Mu'tazilite use of verse 4:14?
A) He says the verse is abrogated.
B) He says it applies only to disbelievers.
C) He interprets 'limits' as the limits of inheritance.
D) He denies that the verse promises eternal fire.

Key Takeaway
Razi shows that the 'limits' in verse 4:14 are contextually linked to inheritance laws, not all sins, thereby refuting the Mu'tazilite proof for eternal punishment of grave sinners.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever interpreted a Quranic verse without considering its context, and then applied it in a way that might mislead yourself or others? What harm could come from that?
?
When you read the Quran, do you actively seek to understand the context of each verse, or do you rely on isolated phrases? How will you change your study habits to ensure you are not like those who misuse the Book of Allah?
?
If you were to defend a theological position using a verse, are you willing to honestly re-examine that verse in its full context, even if it weakens your argument? What is at stake for you personally in doing so?
